https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#

Engineering Manual 1110-1-1005, Control and Topographic Surveying, defines various acronyms and terms commonly used in this instruction to describe survey activities, including technical specifications, procedural guidance, and quality control criteria related to site plans as as-built facility mapping. These terms are defined in the glossary section of the manual.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Absolute_GPS   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Absolute_GPS

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Absolute_GPS is a leaf node.

Description

Operation with a single receiver for a desired position. This receiver may be positioned to be stationary over a point. This mode of positioning is the most common military and civil application.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Accuracy   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Accuracy

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Accuracy is a leaf node.

Description

The degree to which an estimated (mean) value is compatible with an expected value. Accuracy implies the estimated value is unbiased.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Altitude   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Altitude

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Altitude is a leaf node.

Description

The vertical angle between the horizontal plane of the observer and a directional line to the object.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Astronomical_Latitude   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Astronomical_Latitude

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Astronomical_Latitude is a leaf node.

Description

Angle between the plumb line and the plane of celestial equator. Also defined as the angle between the plane of the horizon and the axis of rotation of the earth. Astronomical latitude applies only to positions on the earth and is reckoned from the astronomic equator, north and south through 90E. Astronomical latitude is the latitude that results directly from observations of celestial bodies, uncorrected for deflection of the vertical.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Astronomical_Triangle   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Astronomical_Triangle

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Astronomical_Triangle is a leaf node.

Description

A spherical triangle formed by arcs of great circles connecting the celestial pole, the zenith and a celestial body. The angles of the astronomical triangles are: at the pole, the hour angle; at the celestial body, the parallactic angle; at the zenith, the azimuth angle. The sides are: pole to zenith, the co-latitude; zenith to celestial body, the zenith distance; and celestial body to pole, the polar distance.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Atmospheric_Refraction   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Atmospheric_Refraction

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Atmospheric_Refraction is a leaf node.

Description

Refraction of electromagnetic radiation through the atmosphere causing the line-of-sight to deviate from a straight path. Mainly temperature and pressure conditions determine the magnitude and direction of curvature affecting the path of light from a source. Refraction causes the ray to follow a curved path normal the surface gradient.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Azimuth_Angle   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Azimuth_Angle

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Azimuth_Angle is a leaf node.

Description

The angle less than 180Â° between the plane of the celestial meridian and the vertical plane with the observed object, reckoned from the direction of the elevated pole. In astronomic work, the azimuth angle is the spherical angle at the zenith in the astronomical triangle, which is composed of the pole, the zenith and the star. In geodetic work, it is the horizontal angle between the celestial pole and the observed terrestrial object.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Barometric_Leveling   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Barometric_Leveling

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Barometric_Leveling is a leaf node.

Description

Determining differences of elevation from measured differences of atmospheric pressure observed with a barometer. If the elevation of one station above a datum is known, the approximate elevations of other station can be determined by barometric leveling. Barometric leveling is widely used in reconnaissance and exploratory surveys.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Bureau_International_de_l%27Heure   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Bureau_International_de_l%27Heure

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Bureau_International_de_l%27Heure is a leaf node.

Description

The Bureau was founded in 1919 and its offices since then have been at the Paris Observatory. By an action of the International Astronomical Union, the BIH ceased to exist on 1 January 1988 and a new organization, the International Earth Rotation Service (IERS) was formed to deal with determination of the Earth's rotation.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Cadastral_Survey   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Cadastral_Survey

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Cadastral_Survey is a leaf node.

Description

Relates to land boundaries and subdivisions, and creates units suitable for transfer or to define the limitations of title. The term cadastral survey is now used to designate the surveys of the public lands of the US, including retracement surveys for identification and resurveys for the restoration of property lines; the term can also be applied properly to corresponding surveys outside the public lands, although such surveys are usually termed land surveys through preference.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-1-1005.yaml#term[Cadastral Survey]" ;

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Cartesian_Coordinates   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Cartesian_Coordinates

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Cartesian_Coordinates is a leaf node.

Description

A system with its origin at the center of the earth and the x and y and z axes in the plane of the equator. Typically, the x-axis passes through the meridian of Greenwich, and the z-axis coincides with the earth's axis of rotation. The three axes are mutually orthogonal and form a right-handed system.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Cartesian_System   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Cartesian_System

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Cartesian_System is a leaf node.

Description

A coordinate system consisting of axes intersecting at a common point (origin). The coordinate of a point is the orthogonal distance between that point and the hyperplane determined by all axes. A Cartesian coordinate system has all the axes intersecting at right angles, and the system is called a rectangular.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

An imaginary sphere of infinite radius with the earth as a center. It rotates from east to west on a prolongation of the earth's axis.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Central_Meridian   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Central_Meridian

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Central_Meridian is a leaf node.

Description

A line of constant longitude at the center of a graticule. The central meridian is used as a base for constructing the other lines of the graticule. The meridian is used as the y-axis in computing tables for a State Plane Coordinate system. That line, on a graticule, which represents a meridian and which is an axis of symmetry.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Chart_Datum   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Chart_Datum

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Chart_Datum is a leaf node.

Description

Reference surface for soundings on a nautical chart. It is usually taken to correspond to a low water elevation, and its depression below mean sea level is represented by the symbol Zo. Since 1989, chart datum has been implemented to mean lower low water for all marine waters of the US its territories, Commonwealth of Puerto Rico and Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Confidence_Level   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Confidence_Level

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Confidence_Level is a leaf node.

Description

Statistical probability (in percent) based on the standard deviation or standard error associated with the normal probability density function. The confidence level is assigned according to an expansion factor multiplied by the magnitude of one standard error. The expansion factor is based on values found in probability tables at a chosen level of significance.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Confidence Level" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/portals/76/publications/engineermanuals/em_1110-1-1005.pdf#page=484" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-1-1005.yaml#term[Confidence Level]" ;

    • EM-1110-1-1005:Contour

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Contour is a leaf node.

Description

An imaginary line on the ground with all points at the same elevation above or below a specified reference surface.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Control   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Control

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Control is a leaf node.

Description

Data used in geodesy and cartography to determine the positions and elevations of points on the earth's surface or on a cartographic representation of that surface. A collective term for a system of marks or objects on the earth or on a map or a photograph whose positions or elevation are determined.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Conventional_Terrestrial_Pole_%28CTP%29   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Conventional_Terrestrial_Pole_%28CTP%29

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Conventional_Terrestrial_Pole_%28CTP%29 is a leaf node.

Description

The origin of the WGS 84 Cartesian system is the earth's center of mass. The Z-axis is parallel to the direction of the CTP for polar motion, as defined by the Bureau of International de l'Heure (BIH), and equal to the rotation axis of the WGS 84 ellipsoid. The X-axis is the intersection of the WGS 84 reference meridian plane and the CTP's equator, the reference meridian being parallel to the zero meridian defined by the BIH and equal to the X-axis of the WGS 84 ellipsoid. The Y-axis completes a righthanded, earth-centered, earth-fixed orthogonal coordinate system, measured in the plane of the CTP equator 90 degrees east of the X-axis and equal to the Y-axis of the WGS 84 ellipsoid.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-1-1005:Conventional_Terrestrial_Pole_%28CTP%29 a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Conventional Terrestrial Pole (CTP)" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/portals/76/publications/engineermanuals/em_1110-1-1005.pdf#page=484" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-1-1005.yaml#term[Conventional Terrestrial Pole (CTP)]" ;
skos:definition "The origin of the WGS 84 Cartesian system is the earth's center of mass. The Z-axis is parallel to the direction of the CTP for polar motion, as defined by the Bureau of International de l'Heure (BIH), and equal to the rotation axis of the WGS 84 ellipsoid. The X-axis is the intersection of the WGS 84 reference meridian plane and the CTP's equator, the reference meridian being parallel to the zero meridian defined by the BIH and equal to the X-axis of the WGS 84 ellipsoid. The Y-axis completes a righthanded, earth-centered, earth-fixed orthogonal coordinate system, measured in the plane of the CTP equator 90 degrees east of the X-axis and equal to the Y-axis of the WGS 84 ellipsoid." ;
skos:inScheme EM-1110-1-1005: ;

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Crandall_Method   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Crandall_Method

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Crandall_Method is a leaf node.

Description

Traverse misclosure in azimuth or angle is first distributed in equal portions to all the measured angles. The adjusted angles are then held fixed and all remaining coordinate corrections distributed among the distance measurements.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Curvature   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Curvature

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Curvature is a leaf node.

Description

The rate at which a curve deviates from a straight line. The parametric vector described by dt/ds, where t is the vector tangent to a curve and s is the distance along that curve.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Deflection_of_the_Vertical   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Deflection_of_the_Vertical

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Deflection_of_the_Vertical is a leaf node.

Description

The spatial angular difference between the upward direction of a plumb line and the normal to the reference ellipsoid. Often expressed in two orthogonal components in the meridian and the prime vertical directions.

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Departure is a leaf node.

Description

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Direction   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Direction

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Direction is a leaf node.

Description

The angle between a line or plane and an arbitrarily chosen reference line or plane. At a triangulation station, observed horizontal angles are referred to a common reference line and termed horizontal direction. A line, real or imaginary, pointing away from some specified point or locality toward another point. Direction has two meanings: that of a numerical value and that of a pointing line.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .

@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

    • EM-1110-1-1005:Ellipsoid

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Ellipsoid is a leaf node.

Description

Formed by revolving an ellipse about its minor semi-axis. The most commonly used reference ellipsoids in North America are: Clarke 1866, Geodetic Reference System of 1980 (GRS 80), World Geodetic System of 1972 (WGS 72) and World Geodetic System of 1984 (WGS 84).

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Finite_Element_Method   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Finite_Element_Method

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Finite_Element_Method is a leaf node.

Description

Obtaining an approximate solution to a problem for which the governing differential equations and boundary conditions are known. The method divides the region of interest into numerous, interconnected sub-regions (finite elements) over which simple, approximating functions are used to represent the unknown quantities.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Greenwich_Meridian   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Greenwich_Meridian

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Greenwich_Meridian is a leaf node.

Description

The astronomic meridian through the center of the Airy transit instrument of the Greenwich Observatory, Greenwich, England. By international agreement in 1884, the Greenwich meridian was adopted as the meridian from which all longitudes, worldwide, would be calculated.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Grid_Azimuth   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Grid_Azimuth

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Grid_Azimuth is a leaf node.

Description

The angle in the plane of projection between a straight line and the line (y-axis) in a plane rectangular coordinate system representing the central meridian. While essentially a map-related quantity, a grid azimuth may, by mathematical processes, be transformed into a survey- related or ground-related quantity.

Implementation:

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Intersection   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Intersection

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Intersection is a leaf node.

Description

Determining the horizontal position of a point by observations from two or more points of known position. Thus measuring directions or distances that intersect at the station being located. A station whose horizontal position is located by intersection is known as an intersection station.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Invar   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Invar

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Invar is a leaf node.

Description

An alloy of iron containing nickel, and small amounts of chromium to increase hardness, manganese to facilitate drawing, and carbon to raise the elastic limit, and having a very low coefficient of thermal expansion (about 1/25 that of steel).

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Laplace_Condition   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Laplace_Condition

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Laplace_Condition is a leaf node.

Description

Arises from the fact that a deflection of the vertical in the plane of the prime vertical will give a difference between astronomic and geodetic longitude and between astronomic and geodetic azimuth. Conversely, the observed differences between astronomic and geodetic values of the longitude and of the azimuth may both be used to determine the deflection in the plane of the prime vertical.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Level_Datum   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Level_Datum

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Level_Datum is a leaf node.

Description

A level surface to which elevations are referred. The generally adopted level datum for leveling in the US is mean sea level. For local surveys, an arbitrary level datum is often adopted and defined in terms of an assumed elevation for some physical mark.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Map_Accuracy   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Map_Accuracy

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Map_Accuracy is a leaf node.

Description

The accuracy with which a map represents. Three types of error commonly occur on maps: errors of representation, which occur because conventional signs must be used to represent natural or man-made features such as forests, buildings and cities; errors of identification, which occur because a non-existent feature is shown or is misidentified; and errors of position, which occur when an object is shown in the wrong position. Errors of position are commonly classified into two types: errors of horizontal location and errors of elevation. A third type, often neglected, is errors of orientation.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-1-1005:Map_Accuracy a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Map Accuracy" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/portals/76/publications/engineermanuals/em_1110-1-1005.pdf#page=491" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-1-1005.yaml#term[Map Accuracy]" ;
skos:definition "The accuracy with which a map represents. Three types of error commonly occur on maps: errors of representation, which occur because conventional signs must be used to represent natural or man-made features such as forests, buildings and cities; errors of identification, which occur because a non-existent feature is shown or is misidentified; and errors of position, which occur when an object is shown in the wrong position. Errors of position are commonly classified into two types: errors of horizontal location and errors of elevation. A third type, often neglected, is errors of orientation." ;
skos:inScheme EM-1110-1-1005: ;

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Mean_Sea_Level_Datum is a leaf node.

Description

Adopted as a standard datum for heights or elevations. The Sea Level Datum of 1929, the current standard for geodetic leveling in the United States, is based on tidal observations over a number of years at various tide stations along the coasts.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Micrometer   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Micrometer

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Micrometer is a leaf node.

Description

In general, any instrument for measuring small distances very accurately. In astronomy and geodesy, a device, for attachment to a telescope or microscope, consisting of a mark moved across the field of view by a screw connected to a graduated drum and vernier. If the mark is a hair-like filament, the micrometer is called a filar micrometer.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:NADCON   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:NADCON

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:NADCON is a leaf node.

Description

The National Geodetic Survey developed the conversion program NADCON (North American Datum Conversion) to convert to and from North American Datum of 1983. The technique used is based on a biharmonic equation classically used to model plate deflections. NADCON works exclusively in geographical coordinates (latitude/longitude).

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .

@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-1-1005:NADCON a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "NADCON" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/portals/76/publications/engineermanuals/em_1110-1-1005.pdf#page=492" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-1-1005.yaml#term[NADCON]" ;

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Optical_Micrometer   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Optical_Micrometer

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Optical_Micrometer is a leaf node.

Description

Consists of a prism or lens placed in the path of light entering a telescope and rotatable, by means of a graduated linkage, about a horizontal axis perpendicular to the optical axis of the telescope axis. Also called an optical-mechanical compensator. The device is usually placed in front of the objective of a telescope, but may be placed immediately after it. The parallel-plate optical micrometer is the form usually found in leveling instruments.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-1-1005:Optical_Micrometer a wov:GlossaryTerm,

rdfs:label "Optical Micrometer" ;

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Optical_Plummet   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Optical_Plummet

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Optical_Plummet is a leaf node.

Description

A small telescope having a 90Â° bend in its optical axis and attached to an instrument in such a way that the line of sight proceeds horizontally from the eyepiece to a point on the vertical axis of the instrument and from that point vertically downwards. In use, the observer, looking into the plummet, brings a point on the instrument vertically above a specified point (usually a geodetic or other mark) below it.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Philadelphia_Leveling_Rod   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Philadelphia_Leveling_Rod

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Philadelphia_Leveling_Rod is a leaf node.

Description

Having a target but with graduations so styled that the rod may also be used as a self-reading leveling rod. Also called a Philadelphia rod. If a length greater than 7 feet is needed, the target is clamped at 7 feet and raised by extending the rod. When the target is used, the rod is read by vernier to 0.001 foot. When the rod is used as a self-reading leveling rod, the rod is read to 0.005 foot.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Projection is a leaf node.

Description

A set of functions, or the corresponding geometric constructions, relating points on one surface to points on another surface. A projection requires every point on the first surface to correspond one-to-one to points on the second surface.

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Stadia_Traverse   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Stadia_Traverse

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Stadia_Traverse is a leaf node.

Description

Distances are determined using a stadia rod. A stadia traverse is suited to regions of moderate relief with an adequate network of roads. If done carefully, such a traverse can establish elevations accurate enough for compiling maps with any contour interval now standard.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .

Concept: EM-1110-1-1005:Transit_Rule   back to top

  • skos:Concept
    • EM-1110-1-1005:Transit_Rule

NOTE EM-1110-1-1005:Transit_Rule is a leaf node.

Description

The correction to be applied to the departure (or latitude) of any course has the same ratio to the total misclosure in departure (or latitude) as the departure (latitude) of the course has to the arithmetical sum of all the departures (latitudes) in the traverse. The transit rule is often used when it is believed that the misclosure is caused less by errors in the measured angles than by errors in the measured distances.

Implementation:

@prefix EM-1110-1-1005: <https://usace-data.com/civil-works/glossary/EM-1110-1-1005#> .
@prefix dcterms: <http://purl.org/dc/terms/> .
@prefix pav: <http://purl.org/pav#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .
@prefix skos: <http://www.w3.org/2004/02/skos/core#> .
@prefix wov: <http://www.knowledgesmarts.com/ontologies/wov#> .

EM-1110-1-1005:Transit_Rule a wov:GlossaryTerm,
skos:Concept ;
rdfs:label "Transit Rule" ;
dcterms:bibliographicCitation "https://www.publications.usace.army.mil/portals/76/publications/engineermanuals/em_1110-1-1005.pdf#page=497" ;
pav:wasDerivedFrom "glossaries/CivilWorks/EM-1110-1-1005.yaml#term[Transit Rule]" ;

The transit rule is often used when it is believed that the misclosure is caused less by errors in the measured angles than by errors in the measured distances." ;
